SEC. 1000. DEFINITIONS; SENSE OF CONGRESS. 
3
(a) DEFINITIONS.—In this title: 
4
(1) CULTURALLY CONGRUENT.—The term ‘‘cul-
5
turally congruent’’, with respect to care or maternity 
6
care, means care that is in agreement with the pre-
7
ferred cultural values, beliefs, worldview, language, 
8
and practices of the health care consumer and other 
9
stakeholders. 
10
(2) MATERNITY
CARE
PROVIDER.—The term 
11
‘‘maternity care provider’’ means a health care pro-
12
vider who— 
13
(A) is a physician, physician assistant, 
14
midwife who meets at a minimum the inter-
15
national definition of the midwife and global 
16
standards for midwifery education as estab-
17
lished by the International Confederation of 
18
Midwives, nurse practitioner, or clinical nurse 
19
specialist; and 
20
(B) has a focus on maternal or perinatal 
21
health. 
22
16:38 Sep 26, 2022
H8862
6 
•HR 8862 IH
(3) MATERNAL MORTALITY.—The term ‘‘mater-
1
nal mortality’’ means a death occurring during or 
2
within a one-year period after pregnancy, caused by 
3
pregnancy-related or childbirth complications, in-
4
cluding a suicide, overdose, or other death resulting 
5
from a mental health or substance use disorder at-
6
tributed to or aggravated by pregnancy-related or 
7
childbirth complications. 
8
(4) PERINATAL HEALTH WORKER.—The term 
9
‘‘perinatal health worker’’ means a doula, commu-
10
nity health worker, peer supporter, breastfeeding 
11
and lactation educator or counselor, nutritionist or 
12
dietitian, childbirth educator, social worker, home 
13
visitor, language interpreter, or navigator. 
14
(5) POSTPARTUM AND POSTPARTUM PERIOD.— 
15
The terms ‘‘postpartum’’ and ‘‘postpartum period’’ 
16
refer to the 1-year period beginning on the last day 
17
of the pregnancy of an individual. 
18
(6) 
PREGNANCY-ASSOCIATED
DEATH.—The 
19
term ‘‘pregnancy-associated death’’ means a death of 
20
a pregnant or postpartum individual, by any cause, 
21
that occurs during, or within 1 year following, the 
22
individual’s pregnancy, regardless of the outcome, 
23
duration, or site of the pregnancy. 
24
16:38 Sep 26, 2022
H8862
7 
•HR 8862 IH
(7) PREGNANCY-RELATED
DEATH.—The term 
1
‘‘pregnancy-related death’’ means a death of a preg-
2
nant or postpartum individual that occurs during, or 
3
within 1 year following, the individual’s pregnancy, 
4
from a pregnancy complication, a chain of events 
5
initiated by pregnancy, or the aggravation of an un-
6
related condition by the physiologic effects of preg-
7
nancy. 
8
(8) RACIAL AND ETHNIC MINORITY GROUP.— 
9
The term ‘‘racial and ethnic minority group’’ has the 
10
meaning given such term in section 1707(g)(1) of 
11
the Public Health Service Act (42 U.S.C. 300u– 
12
6(g)(1)). 
13
(9) SEVERE MATERNAL MORBIDITY.—The term 
14
‘‘severe maternal morbidity’’ means a health condi-
15
tion, including mental health conditions and sub-
16
stance use disorders, attributed to or aggravated by 
17
pregnancy or childbirth that results in significant 
18
short-term or long-term consequences to the health 
19
of the individual who was pregnant. 
20
(10) SOCIAL
DETERMINANTS
OF
MATERNAL 
21
HEALTH DEFINED.—The term ‘‘social determinants 
22
of maternal health’’ means non-clinical factors that 
23
impact maternal health outcomes, including— 
24
16:38 Sep 26, 2022
H8862
8 
•HR 8862 IH
(A) economic factors, which may include 
1
poverty, employment, food security, support for 
2
and access to lactation and other infant feeding 
3
options, housing stability, and related factors; 
4
(B) neighborhood factors, which may in-
5
clude quality of housing, access to transpor-
6
tation, access to child care, availability of 
7
healthy foods and nutrition counseling, avail-
8
ability of clean water, air and water quality, 
9

10
violence, access to broadband, and related fac-
11
tors; 
12
(C) social and community factors, which 
13
may include systemic racism, gender discrimi-
14
nation or discrimination based on other pro-
15
tected classes, workplace conditions, incarcer-
16
ation, and related factors; 
17
(D) household factors, which may include 
18
ability to conduct lead testing and abatement, 
19
car seat installation, indoor air temperatures, 
20
and related factors; 
21
(E) education access and quality factors, 
22
which may include educational attainment, lan-
23
guage and literacy, and related factors; and 
24
16:38 Sep 26, 2022

9 
•HR 8862 IH
(F) health care access factors, including 
1

ment programs, health literacy, access to tele-

7
services, and related factors.

SEC. 1002. HOUSING FOR MOMS GRANT PROGRAM. 
6
(a) IN GENERAL.—The Secretary of Housing and 
7

16

17
(c) PRIORITY.—In awarding grants under this sec-
18

19

24

SEC. 4002. PAYMENTS TO POSSESSIONS. 
1
(a) MIRROR CODE POSSESSION.—The Secretary of 
2
the Treasury shall pay to each possession of the United 
3
States with a mirror code tax system amounts equal to 
4
the loss to that possession by reason of the application 
5
of section 36C of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 (as 
6
added by section 4001) with respect to taxable years be-
7
ginning after 2020. Such amounts shall be determined by 
8
the Secretary of the Treasury based on information pro-
9
vided by the government of the respective possession. 
10
(b) OTHER POSSESSIONS.—The Secretary of the 
11
Treasury shall pay to each possession of the United States 
12
which does not have a mirror code tax system amounts 
13
estimated by the Secretary of the Treasury as being equal 
14
to the aggregate benefits that would have been provided 
15
to residents of such possession by reason of the application 
16
of section 36C of such Code (as so added) for taxable 
17
years beginning after 2021 if a mirror code tax system 
18
had been in effect in such possession. The preceding sen-
19
tence shall not apply with respect to any possession of the 
20
United States unless such possession has a plan, which 
21
has been approved by the Secretary of the Treasury, under 
22
which such possession will promptly distribute such pay-
23
ments to the residents of such possession. 
24

SEC. 6001. DEFINITIONS.

In this title:

(1) EMPLOYEE; EMPLOYER.—The terms ‘‘em-
9
ployee’’ and ‘‘employer’’ have the meanings given 
10

11

13

(3) SERIOUS HEALTH CONDITION.—The term 
15
‘‘serious health condition’’ has the meaning given 
16
such term in section 101 of the Family and Medical 
17
Leave Act of 1993 (29 U.S.C. 2611). 
18
SEC. 6002. CERTIFICATION PROGRAM ESTABLISHED. 
19
(a) IN GENERAL.—The Secretary shall establish a 
20
national certification program to award certifications to 
21
recognize employers that have a commitment to helping 
22
employees balance employment responsibilities and family 
23
obligations (referred to in this section as ‘‘family-friendly 
24
certifications’’). 
25
16:38 Sep 26, 2022
H8862
289 
•HR 8862 IH
(b) CRITERIA FOR CERTIFICATION.—In order to be 
1
eligible to receive a family-friendly certification, an em-
2
ployer shall carry out each of the following family-friendly 
3
employment policies and benefits: 
4
(1) Assistance paying for, or referring employ-
5
ees to, fertility or adoption services. 
6
(2) Paid family leave of not less than 12 weeks 
7
per year, including the option to use leave for any 
8
of the following reasons: 
9
(A) The birth of a child of the employee 
10
and in order to care for such child. 
11
(B) The placement of a child with the em-
12
ployee for adoption or foster care. 
13
(C) To address the serious health condi-
14
tion, including pregnancy, childbirth, or preg-
15
nancy loss, of the employee. 
16
(D) To address the serious health condi-
17
tion of a family member. 
18
(E) For specific military caregiving and 
19
leave. 
20
(3) Paid sick days for employees that are sepa-
21
rate from time accrued as part of a paid time off 
22
policy. 
23
16:38 Sep 26, 2022
H8862
290 
•HR 8862 IH
(4) A subsidy for child care or policies that 
1
allow parents to work alongside their infants in safe 
2
settings. 
3
(5) Policies that allow for flexible hours once a 
4
parent returns to work after a birth, adoption, or 
5
foster care placement. 
6
(6) If feasible, policies that allow employees to 
7
work remotely as needed for reasons related to the 
8
care of a child. 
9
(7) Lactation support, such as reimbursement 
10
of expressed breastmilk delivery while on travel, ac-
11

12

13
support. 
14

15
ceive a family-friendly certification from the Secretary 
16

17

18
